<div class="marriage-display-ws"><div style="display:inline-block;line-height:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Offset_(rapper)" title="Offset (rapper)">Offset</a></div>&#32;<div style="display:inline-block;">&#8203;</div>&#40;<abbr title="married">m.</abbr>&#160;2017&#41;<wbr />&#8203;</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data">2</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Awards</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Cardi_B" title="List of awards and nominations received by Cardi B">Full list</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><b>Musical career</b></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Genres</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Hip hop</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Trap_music" title="Trap music">trap</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Instrument(s)</th><td class="infobox-data note">Vocals</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Labels</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist"><ul><li>KSR<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></li><li><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://Cardib.com">cardib<wbr />.com</a></span>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardi_B_logo.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Cardi_B_logo.png/200px-Cardi_B_logo.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Cardi_B_logo.png/300px-Cardi_B_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Cardi_B_logo.png/400px-Cardi_B_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="545" data-file-height="69" /></a></span></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Belcalis Marlenis Almánzar Cephus</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/ɑːr/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;far&#39;">ɑːr</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[alˈmansaɾ]</a></span>; born October 11, 1992), known professionally as <b>Cardi B</b>, is an American rapper. According to various media outlets, she is regarded as one of the most commercially successful female rappers of her generation. She has received several <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Cardi_B" title="List of awards and nominations received by Cardi B"> accolades</a> including a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>, eight <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" title="Billboard Music Awards">Billboard Music Awards</a>, six <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>, six <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, and  fourteen <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>. 
</p><p>In 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine included her on its <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">annual list</a> of the 100 most influential people in the world, and in 2020, <i>Billboard</i> honored her as <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music#Woman_of_the_Year_Award" title="Billboard Women in Music">Woman of the Year</a>. Outside of music, she became the <a href="/wiki/Creative_director" title="Creative director">creative director</a> of entertainment magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Playboy (magazine)">Playboy</a></i> in 2022. 
</p><p>Born and raised in New York City, she first gained popularity through <a href="/wiki/Vine_(service)" title="Vine (service)">Vine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a>. From 2015 to early 2017, she appeared as a regular cast member on the <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> reality television series <i><a href="/wiki/Love_%26_Hip_Hop:_New_York" title="Love &amp; Hip Hop: New York">Love &amp; Hip Hop: New York</a></i>, which depicted her pursuit of her music aspirations, and earned further recognition with the release of her two <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtapes</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Bitch_Music,_Vol._1" title="Gangsta Bitch Music, Vol. 1">Gangsta Bitch Music, Vol. 1</a></i> (2016) and <i><a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Bitch_Music,_Vol._2" title="Gangsta Bitch Music, Vol. 2">Vol. 2</a></i> (2017).
</p><p>Her first studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Privacy_(album)" title="Invasion of Privacy (album)">Invasion of Privacy</a></i> (2018), debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and was ranked the top female rap album of the 2010s by <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>. Critically acclaimed, it made Cardi B the first female artist to win the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Grammy Award for Best Rap Album</a> as a solo artist, and marked the first female rap album in 15 years nominated for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>. It spawned two number-one singles on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i> Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>; with "<a href="/wiki/Bodak_Yellow" title="Bodak Yellow">Bodak Yellow</a>", its lead single, Cardi B became the first female rapper to top the Hot 100 with a solo song in the 21st century and the first to achieve a <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification#RIAA_Diamond_certifications" title="RIAA certification">diamond</a>-certified song by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>, while "<a href="/wiki/I_Like_It_(Cardi_B,_Bad_Bunny_and_J_Balvin_song)" title="I Like It (Cardi B, Bad Bunny and J Balvin song)">I Like It</a>" marked the first time a female rapper attained multiple number-one songs on the Hot 100. Her third Hot 100 number-one, the collaboration "<a href="/wiki/Girls_Like_You" title="Girls Like You">Girls Like You</a>" with band <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a>, made her the only female rapper to achieve multiple diamond-certified songs by the RIAA. She has since released two singles: "<a href="/wiki/WAP_(song)" title="WAP (song)">WAP</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Megan_Thee_Stallion" title="Megan Thee Stallion">Megan Thee Stallion</a>) in 2020 and "<a href="/wiki/Up_(Cardi_B_song)" title="Up (Cardi B song)">Up</a>" in 2021, both of which topped the Hot 100 and other charts worldwide.
</p><p>Recognized by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> as one of the most influential female rappers of all time, Cardi B holds various records among women in hip hop; she is <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">the female rapper with the most number-one singles</a> (five) on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, the only to achieve multiple solo number ones and the only to earn number ones in two decades (2010s and 2020s) on the chart.  She is also the female rapper with the most diamond-certified songs (three) by the RIAA, the highest-certified female rapper of all time on <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-certified_music_artists_in_the_United_States" title="List of highest-certified music artists in the United States">their Top Artists (Digital Singles)</a> ranking, and has 100 million certified units (album and songs) sold in the US alone. Additionally, she is the female rapper with the most songs with <a href="/wiki/List_of_most-streamed_songs_on_Spotify" class="mw-redirect" title="List of most-streamed songs on Spotify">a billion streams</a> on <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a>—where she also has the most-streamed female rap album. She was the first lead artist to top the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Global_200" title="Billboard Global 200"><i>Billboard</i> Global 200</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Belcalis Marlenis Almánzar was born on October 11, 1992, in the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Heights,_Manhattan" title="Washington Heights, Manhattan">Washington Heights</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tweet_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tweet-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vogue_cover_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue_cover-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Her father Carlos is <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Americans" title="Dominican Americans">Dominican</a> and her mother Clara is a <a href="/wiki/Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian_Americans" title="Trinidadian and Tobagonian Americans">Trinidadian</a> of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Trinidadians_and_Tobagonians" title="Afro-Trinidadians and Tobagonians">African</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish</a> descent; Almánzar identifies as an <a href="/wiki/Black_Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Black Hispanic and Latino Americans">Afro-Latina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tweet_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tweet-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Almánzar was raised in the <a href="/wiki/Highbridge,_Bronx" title="Highbridge, Bronx">Highbridge</a> neighborhood of the <a href="/wiki/South_Bronx" title="South Bronx">South Bronx</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and spent much time at her paternal grandmother's home in Washington Heights, which she credits with giving her "such a thick accent."<sup id="cite_ref-five_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-five-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Almánzar developed the stage name "Cardi B" as a derivation of <a href="/wiki/Bacardi" title="Bacardi">Bacardi</a>, a rum brand that was formerly her nickname.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> She has a younger sister, Hennessy Carolina, who was born in 1995. She has said she was a gang member with the <a href="/wiki/United_Blood_Nation" title="United Blood Nation">Bloods</a> in her youth, since age 16,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> but stated she would not encourage joining a gang.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> She attended Renaissance High School for Musical Theater &amp; Technology, a <a href="/wiki/Vocational_high_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Vocational high school">vocational high school</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Herbert_H._Lehman_High_School" title="Herbert H. Lehman High School">Herbert H. Lehman High School</a> campus.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During her teens, Cardi B was employed at an Amish deli in <a href="/wiki/Tribeca" title="Tribeca">Tribeca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Decker_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decker-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> She was fired and became a dancer at a strip club across the street.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CBSCL_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSCL-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B has said that becoming a stripper was positive for her life in many ways: "It really saved me from a lot of things. When I started stripping I went back to school."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> She stated that she became a stripper to escape poverty and <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a>, having been in an abusive relationship at the time after being kicked out of her mother's house,<sup id="cite_ref-vibe_viva_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibe_viva-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and that stripping was her only way to earn enough money to escape the situation and get an education.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> She attended <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Manhattan_Community_College" title="Borough of Manhattan Community College">Borough of Manhattan Community College</a><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> before eventually dropping out.<sup id="cite_ref-complex1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex1-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> While stripping, Cardi B lied to her mother by telling her she was making money by <a href="/wiki/Babysitting" title="Babysitting">babysitting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30_Eccentric_Facts_About_Cardi_B_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30_Eccentric_Facts_About_Cardi_B-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, she began to gain publicity due to several of her videos spreading on social media, on <a href="/wiki/Vine_(service)" title="Vine (service)">Vine</a> and her <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> page.<sup id="cite_ref-fader1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader1-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="2015.E2.80.932016:_Career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–2016:_Career_beginnings">2015–2016: Career beginnings</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardi_B_2016.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Cardi_B_2016.jpg/170px-Cardi_B_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Cardi_B_2016.jpg/255px-Cardi_B_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Cardi_B_2016.jpg/340px-Cardi_B_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="558" /></a><figcaption>Cardi B being interviewed on <i><a href="/wiki/Lisa_Evers" title="Lisa Evers">Street Soldiers with Lisa Evers</a></i> in January 2016</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2015, Cardi B joined the cast of the <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> reality television series <i><a href="/wiki/Love_%26_Hip_Hop:_New_York" title="Love &amp; Hip Hop: New York">Love &amp; Hip Hop: New York</a></i>, debuting in season six.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Jezebel_(website)" title="Jezebel (website)">Jezebel</a></i> considered her the breakout star of the show's sixth season.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> wrote that she garnered popularity with "her ability to rattle off one-liners".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The sixth and seventh seasons chronicle her rise to stardom and her turbulent relationship with her incarcerated fiancé. On December 30, 2016, after two seasons, she announced that she would be leaving the show to further pursue a career in music.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2015, Cardi B made her musical debut on Jamaican <a href="/wiki/Reggae_fusion" title="Reggae fusion">reggae fusion</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Shaggy_(musician)" title="Shaggy (musician)">Shaggy</a>'s remix to his single "Boom Boom", alongside fellow Jamaican <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Popcaan" title="Popcaan">Popcaan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-boomboom_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boomboom-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> She made her music video debut on December 15, 2015, with the song "Cheap Ass Weave", her rendition of British <a href="/wiki/Rapper" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapper">rapper</a> <a href="/wiki/Lady_Leshurr" title="Lady Leshurr">Lady Leshurr</a>'s "Queen's Speech 4".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On March 7, 2016, Cardi B released her first full-length project, a <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Bitch_Music,_Vol._1" title="Gangsta Bitch Music, Vol. 1">Gangsta Bitch Music, Vol. 1</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In November 2016, she was featured on the digital cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> magazine<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s "Viva" issue.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vibe_viva_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibe_viva-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 12, 2016, KSR Group released the compilation <i>Underestimated: The Album</i>, which is a collaboration between KSR Group artists Cardi B, <a href="/wiki/HoodCelebrityy" title="HoodCelebrityy">HoodCelebrityy</a>, SwiftOnDemand, Cashflow Harlem, and <a href="/wiki/Josh_X" title="Josh X">Josh X</a>. It was previously released only to attendees of their U.S. tour. KSR Group's flagship artist Cardi B said "I wanted to make a song that would make girls dance, <a href="/wiki/Twerk" class="mw-redirect" title="Twerk">twerk</a> and at the same time encourage them to go get that Shmoney," in regard to the compilation's single "What a Girl Likes".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She appeared on the December 9, 2015, episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Uncommon_Sense_with_Charlamagne" title="Uncommon Sense with Charlamagne">Uncommon Sense with Charlamagne</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On April 6, 2016, she was on the twelfth episode of <a href="/wiki/Khlo%C3%A9_Kardashian" title="Khloé Kardashian">Khloé Kardashian</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Kocktails_with_Khlo%C3%A9" title="Kocktails with Khloé">Kocktails with Khloé</a></i>: in this episode, she revealed how she told her mother that she was a stripper.<sup id="cite_ref-fyi_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fyi-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In November 2016, it was announced that she would be joining the cast of the <a href="/wiki/BET" title="BET">BET</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Being_Mary_Jane" title="Being Mary Jane">Being Mary Jane</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/TVLine" title="TVLine">TVLine</a> describes her character, Mercedes, as a "round-the-way beauty with a big weave, big boobs and a big booty to match her oversize, ratchet personality."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-latina_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latina-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Cardi B was featured in her first endorsement deal with <a href="/wiki/Romantic_Depot" title="Romantic Depot">Romantic Depot</a>, a large New York chain of lingerie stores that sell sexual health and wellness products. The ad campaign was featured on radio and cable TV.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2017.E2.80.932018:_Breakthrough_with_Invasion_of_Privacy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–2018:_Breakthrough_with_Invasion_of_Privacy">2017–2018: Breakthrough with <i>Invasion of Privacy</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardi_B_at_the_VMAs_2018.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Cardi_B_at_the_VMAs_2018.jpg/170px-Cardi_B_at_the_VMAs_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="213" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Cardi_B_at_the_VMAs_2018.jpg/255px-Cardi_B_at_the_VMAs_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Cardi_B_at_the_VMAs_2018.jpg/340px-Cardi_B_at_the_VMAs_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="529" data-file-height="662" /></a><figcaption>Cardi B at the <a href="/wiki/2018_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2018 MTV Video Music Awards">2018 MTV Video Music Awards</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>On January 20, 2017, Cardi B released her second mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Bitch_Music,_Vol._2" title="Gangsta Bitch Music, Vol. 2">Gangsta Bitch Music, Vol. 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In February 2017, Cardi B partnered with <a href="/wiki/MAC_Cosmetics" title="MAC Cosmetics">MAC Cosmetics</a> and Rio Uribe's <a href="/wiki/Gypsy_Sport" title="Gypsy Sport">Gypsy Sport</a> for an event for <a href="/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week" title="New York Fashion Week">New York Fashion Week</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYFW_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYFW-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In late February, Cardi B signed her first major record label recording contract with <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On February 25, 2017, Cardi B was the <a href="/wiki/Opening_act" title="Opening act">opening act</a> for <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_hip_hop" title="East Coast hip hop">East Coast hip hop</a> group <a href="/wiki/The_Lox" title="The Lox">The Lox</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Filthy_America..._It%27s_Beautiful" title="Filthy America... It&#39;s Beautiful">Filthy America... It's Beautiful</a> Tour, alongside fellow New York City-based rappers <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim" title="Lil&#39; Kim">Lil' Kim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Remy_Ma" title="Remy Ma">Remy Ma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In April 2017, she was featured in <i><a href="/wiki/I-D" title="I-D">i-D</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "A-Z of Music" video sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Marc_Jacobs" title="Marc Jacobs">Marc Jacobs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Cardi guest-starred on the celebrity <a href="/wiki/Panel_show" title="Panel show">panel show</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Squares" title="Hip Hop Squares">Hip Hop Squares</a></i>, appearing on the March 13 and April 3, 2017, episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> She also released the <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyle</a> "Red Barz".<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2017, the nominees for the <a href="/wiki/2017_BET_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2017 BET Awards">2017 BET Awards</a> were announced, revealing that Cardi B had been nominated for <a href="/wiki/BET_Award_for_Best_New_Artist" title="BET Award for Best New Artist">Best New Artist</a> and <a href="/wiki/BET_Award_for_Best_Female_Hip-Hop_Artist" class="mw-redirect" title="BET Award for Best Female Hip-Hop Artist">Best Female Hip-Hop Artist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Chance_the_Rapper" title="Chance the Rapper">Chance the Rapper</a> and Remy Ma won those categories, respectively, Cardi B performed at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a> <a href="/wiki/Party#After-party" title="Party">Afterparty</a> show.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On June 11, 2017, during <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a>'s annual <a href="/wiki/Summer_Jam_(festival)" title="Summer Jam (festival)">Summer Jam</a> music festival, Remy Ma brought out Cardi B, along with <a href="/wiki/The_Lady_of_Rage" title="The Lady of Rage">The Lady of Rage</a>, <a href="/wiki/MC_Lyte" title="MC Lyte">MC Lyte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_M.A" title="Young M.A">Young M.A</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monie_Love" title="Monie Love">Monie Love</a>, Lil' Kim, and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a>, to celebrate female rappers and perform Latifah's 1993 hit single "<a href="/wiki/U.N.I.T.Y." title="U.N.I.T.Y.">U.N.I.T.Y.</a>" about <a href="/wiki/Female_empowerment" class="mw-redirect" title="Female empowerment">female empowerment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In June 2017, it was revealed that Cardi B would be on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fader" title="The Fader">The Fader</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Summer Music issue for July/August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> She performed at <a href="/wiki/MoMA_PS1" title="MoMA PS1">MoMA PS1</a> on August 19 to a crowd of 4,000.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 16, 2017, Atlantic Records released Cardi B's commercial debut single, "<a href="/wiki/Bodak_Yellow" title="Bodak Yellow">Bodak Yellow</a>", via <a href="/wiki/Digital_distribution" title="Digital distribution">digital distribution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> She performed the single on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wendy_Williams_Show" title="The Wendy Williams Show">The Wendy Williams Show</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-ww_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">Jimmy Kimmel Live!</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The song climbed the charts for several months, and, on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart dated September 25, 2017, "Bodak Yellow" reached the number one spot, making Cardi B the first female rapper to do so with a solo single since <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Doo_Wop_(That_Thing)" title="Doo Wop (That Thing)">Doo Wop (That Thing)</a>" debuted atop the chart in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The song stayed atop the charts for three consecutive weeks, tying with American pop singer <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Look_What_You_Made_Me_Do" title="Look What You Made Me Do">Look What You Made Me Do</a>" as the longest running female at the number one spot in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B became the first person of Dominican descent to reach number one in the history of the Hot 100 since it was launched in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> An editor of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> called it "the rap anthem of the summer".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Selected by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i> music critics as the best song of 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> "Bodak Yellow" was eventually certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">Diamond</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA). The song received nominations for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Performance">Best Rap Performance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Song">Best Rap Song</a> at the <a href="/wiki/60th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="60th Annual Grammy Awards">60th Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-grammys_2018_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammys_2018-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> It won Single of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/2017_BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="2017 BET Hip Hop Awards">2017 BET Hip Hop Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With her collaborations "<a href="/wiki/No_Limit_(G-Eazy_song)" title="No Limit (G-Eazy song)">No Limit</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/MotorSport" title="MotorSport">MotorSport</a>", she became the first female rapper to land her first three entries in the top 10 of the Hot 100,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and the first female artist to achieve the same on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In October 2017, Cardi B headlined <a href="/wiki/Power_105.1" class="mw-redirect" title="Power 105.1">Power 105.1</a>'s annual Powerhouse music celebration, alongside <a href="/wiki/The_Weeknd" title="The Weeknd">the Weeknd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Migos" title="Migos">Migos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Uzi_Vert" title="Lil Uzi Vert">Lil Uzi Vert</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a> in Brooklyn, New York.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In December, she released two songs: a collaboration with Puerto Rican singer <a href="/wiki/Ozuna_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ozuna (singer)">Ozuna</a> titled "<a href="/wiki/La_Modelo_(Ozuna_song)" title="La Modelo (Ozuna song)">La Modelo</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/Bartier_Cardi" title="Bartier Cardi">Bartier Cardi</a>", the second single from her <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Privacy_(album)" title="Invasion of Privacy (album)">debut album.</a><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardi_B_Photo_by_Chris_Allmeid_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Cardi_B_Photo_by_Chris_Allmeid_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Cardi_B_Photo_by_Chris_Allmeid_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="216" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Cardi_B_Photo_by_Chris_Allmeid_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Cardi_B_Photo_by_Chris_Allmeid_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Cardi_B_Photo_by_Chris_Allmeid_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Cardi_B_Photo_by_Chris_Allmeid_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1144" data-file-height="1454" /></a><figcaption>Cardi B backstage at the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Jingle_Ball" class="mw-redirect" title="Jingle Ball">Jingle Ball</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>On January 3, 2018, Cardi B was featured on <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Mars" title="Bruno Mars">Bruno Mars</a>' <a href="/wiki/Finesse_(Bruno_Mars_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Finesse (Bruno Mars song)">remix version of "Finesse"</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> and appeared in the 90s inspired video. It reached the top three on the Hot 100, Canada and New Zealand. On January 18, 2018, Cardi B became the first woman to have five top 10 singles simultaneously on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs chart.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> She released another single, "<a href="/wiki/Be_Careful_(Cardi_B_song)" title="Be Careful (Cardi B song)">Be Careful</a>", on March 30, 2018, a week before her album's release.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Her debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Privacy_(album)" title="Invasion of Privacy (album)">Invasion of Privacy</a></i>, was released on April 6, 2018, to universal acclaim from music critics.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Editors from <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> called it "one of the most powerful debuts of this millennium" and "a hip-hop album that doesn't sound like any of its temporal peers," respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tnyt_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tnyt-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The album entered at number one in the United States, while she became the first female artist to chart 13 entries simultaneously on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, on the chart issue dated April 21.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> It became the most <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streamed</a> album by a female artist in a single week in <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music" title="Apple Music">Apple Music</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and the largest on-demand audio streaming week ever for an album by a woman.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Cardi held the latter record <a href="/wiki/Thank_U,_Next" title="Thank U, Next">until 2019</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The album's title reflects Cardi B's feeling that as she gained popularity her privacy was being invaded in a variety of ways.<sup id="cite_ref-Decker_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decker-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Following the album's release, during a performance on <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, Cardi B officially announced her pregnancy, after much media speculation.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> She also co-hosted an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several months later, in July 2018, the album's fourth single, "<a href="/wiki/I_Like_It_(Cardi_B,_Bad_Bunny_and_J_Balvin_song)" title="I Like It (Cardi B, Bad Bunny and J Balvin song)">I Like It</a>", which features vocals from <a href="/wiki/Bad_Bunny" title="Bad Bunny">Bad Bunny</a> and <a href="/wiki/J_Balvin" title="J Balvin">J Balvin</a>, reached number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a>; this marked her second number one on the chart and made her the first female rapper to achieve multiple chart-toppers.<sup id="cite_ref-I_like_it_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I_like_it-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> It received critical acclaim,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> naming it "the <a href="/wiki/Song_of_the_summer" title="Song of the summer">best summer song</a> of all time" in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Her collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Girls_Like_You" title="Girls Like You">Girls Like You</a>", also reached number one on the Hot 100 chart, extending her record among female rappers<sup id="cite_ref-Girls_Like_You_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Girls_Like_You-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> and also making her the sixth female artist to achieve three number-one singles on the chart during the 2010s.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The song's music video has received more than 3&#160;billion views on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> and was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles" title="List of best-selling singles">fifth-best selling song</a> of the year globally.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With "Girls Like You" following "I Like It" at the top of the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay_(Radio_Songs)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 100 Airplay (Radio Songs)">Radio Songs</a> chart, Cardi B became the <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay_(Radio_Songs)#Self-replacement_at_number_one" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 100 Airplay (Radio Songs)">first female rapper</a> to ever replace herself at number one on that chart.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The single spent seven weeks atop the Hot 100, making Cardi the female rapper with the most cumulative weeks atop the chart, with eleven weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-hot_100_11_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hot_100_11-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trust_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trust-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> It spent 33 weeks in the top 10, tying both <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sheeran" title="Ed Sheeran">Ed Sheeran</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Shape_of_You" title="Shape of You">Shape of You</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Post_Malone" title="Post Malone">Post Malone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swae_Lee" title="Swae Lee">Swae Lee</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Sunflower_(Post_Malone_and_Swae_Lee_song)" title="Sunflower (Post Malone and Swae Lee song)">Sunflower</a>" for the longest top 10 run in the chart's archives at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In October 2018, <i>Invasion of Privacy</i> was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_Certification" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA Certification">double platinum</a> by the RIAA, and the following year it was updated to triple platinum. With the thirteen tracks, she became the first female artist to have all songs from an album certified gold or higher in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmes_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B received the most nominations for the <a href="/wiki/2018_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2018 MTV Video Music Awards">2018 MTV Video Music Awards</a> with 12 mentions—including for <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year" title="MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year">Video of the Year</a>, winning three awards.<sup id="cite_ref-vmas_2018_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vmas_2018-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> She tied with <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a> for the most nominations at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2018" title="American Music Awards of 2018">2018 American Music Awards</a>. She won three AMAs and performed at the ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-amas_2018_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amas_2018-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Her single "<a href="/wiki/Money_(Cardi_B_song)" title="Money (Cardi B song)">Money</a>" earned her a fourth Video Music Award, with visuals that feature Cardi playing characters in different locations, including in an art museum, a bank and a strip club.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmes_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Her collaboration with <a href="/wiki/DJ_Snake" title="DJ Snake">DJ Snake</a> "<a href="/wiki/Taki_Taki_(song)" title="Taki Taki (song)">Taki Taki</a>" topped the charts in a number of Hispanic countries, made Cardi B the first female rapper to top the Spotify <a href="/wiki/List_of_most-streamed_songs_on_Spotify#Weekly_number-one_songs" class="mw-redirect" title="List of most-streamed songs on Spotify">Global 50</a> chart,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> and has garnered more than 2&#160;billion views. Both singles were certified multiple-platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa_list_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa_list-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/People_en_Espa%C3%B1ol" title="People en Español">People en Español</a></i> named her Star of the Year,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> deemed her "a pop culture phenomenon", as she was named one of "2018 Entertainers of the Year".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 30, 2018, Cardi B was honored at <i><a href="/wiki/Ebony_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebony Magazine">Ebony</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s annual Power 100 Gala.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Cardi ranked fifth on the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Year-End" title="Billboard Year-End"><i>Billboard</i> Year-End</a> Top Artists chart, while <i>Invasion of Privacy</i> ranked sixth. She achieved the most-streamed album of the year by a female artist globally in <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music" title="Apple Music">Apple Music</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> and ranked as the most streamed female artist of the year in the United States in <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Editorial staff from Apple Music and <i>Billboard</i> named "I Like It" the best song of 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i> magazine</a> and <i>Rolling Stone</i> named <i>Invasion of Privacy</i> the best album of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2018, <i>Time</i> included her on their <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">annual list</a> of the 100 most influential people in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-time_100_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time_100-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In its decade-end review article, <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> stated that the era secured "her crown as the new <a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Queen of Rap</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-nme_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nme-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2019.E2.80.932020:_Hustlers.2C_Rhythm_.2B_Flow_and_WAP"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–2020:_Hustlers,_Rhythm_+_Flow_and_WAP">2019–2020: <i>Hustlers</i>, <i>Rhythm + Flow</i> and <i>WAP</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardi_B_-_Openair_Frauenfeld_2019_02.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Cardi_B_-_Openair_Frauenfeld_2019_02.jpg/170px-Cardi_B_-_Openair_Frauenfeld_2019_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="207" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Cardi_B_-_Openair_Frauenfeld_2019_02.jpg/255px-Cardi_B_-_Openair_Frauenfeld_2019_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Cardi_B_-_Openair_Frauenfeld_2019_02.jpg/340px-Cardi_B_-_Openair_Frauenfeld_2019_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2063" data-file-height="2510" /></a><figcaption>Cardi B performing at the <a href="/wiki/Openair_Frauenfeld" title="Openair Frauenfeld">Openair Frauenfeld</a> in July 2019</figcaption></figure>
<p>Cardi B received five nominations at the <a href="/wiki/61st_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="61st Annual Grammy Awards">61st Grammy Awards</a>, including for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a> ("I Like It").<sup id="cite_ref-grammy_noms_2019_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammy_noms_2019-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> She became the third female rapper to be nominated for Album of the Year, following <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a> (1999) and <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> (2004).<sup id="cite_ref-iop_aoty_nom_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iop_aoty_nom-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> On February 10, 2019, she then performed at the award ceremony, where she wore three vintage <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Mugler" title="Thierry Mugler">Thierry Mugler</a> couture looks during the telecast and became the first female rapper to win <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> as a solo artist.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B led the <a href="/wiki/2019_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2019 Billboard Music Awards">2019 Billboard Music Awards</a> nominations, with 21, the most nominations in a single year ever by a woman and the third most nominations in a year ever (behind Drake and The Chainsmokers, who both had 22 in a year).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> She ended up winning six awards, including for <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award_for_Top_Hot_100_Song" title="Billboard Music Award for Top Hot 100 Song">Top Hot 100 Song</a>, bringing her career total wins to seven—the most of any female rapper in history.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> An article by <i><a href="/wiki/Omaha_World-Herald" title="Omaha World-Herald">Omaha World-Herald</a></i> called her "the biggest rapper in the world."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 15, 2019, Cardi B released "<a href="/wiki/Please_Me" title="Please Me">Please Me</a>", a collaboration with Bruno Mars, which became her seventh top-ten song on the Hot 100, reaching number three.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The song marked Cardi and Bruno's second collaboration, following "<a href="/wiki/Finesse_(song)" title="Finesse (song)">Finesse</a>" in 2018. The official music video was released two weeks later.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> On March 1, Cardi set a new attendance record at the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Livestock_Show_and_Rodeo" title="Houston Livestock Show and Rodeo">Houston Livestock Show and Rodeo</a>, with 75,580 fans in the audience.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> With "<a href="/wiki/Backin%27_It_Up" title="Backin&#39; It Up">Backin' It Up</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Twerk_(City_Girls_song)" title="Twerk (City Girls song)">Twerk</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Money_(Cardi_B_song)" title="Money (Cardi B song)">Money</a>", Cardi became the first female artist to occupy the top three on the <i>Billboard</i> Mainstream R&amp;B/Hip-Hop airplay chart.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Her following single titled "<a href="/wiki/Press_(Cardi_B_song)" title="Press (Cardi B song)">Press</a>" was released on May 31, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Parental_Advisory" title="Parental Advisory">parental-advisory</a> labeled music video marked her directorial debut—being credited as co-director, and was released on June 26, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> It had its debut performance at the <a href="/wiki/2019_BET_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 BET Awards">2019 BET Awards</a>, where she received the most nominations with seven, and won <a href="/wiki/BET_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="BET Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> During the summer of 2019, she embarked on an arena tour.<sup id="cite_ref-arena_19_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arena_19-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In September, she led the <a href="/wiki/2019_BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="2019 BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a> nominations with ten.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B made her film debut in <i><a href="/wiki/Hustlers_(film)" title="Hustlers (film)">Hustlers</a></i> directed by <a href="/wiki/Lorene_Scafaria" title="Lorene Scafaria">Lorene Scafaria</a>, opposite <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constance_Wu" title="Constance Wu">Constance Wu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lili_Reinhart" title="Lili Reinhart">Lili Reinhart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The film was released on September 13, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B, along with <a href="/wiki/Chance_the_Rapper" title="Chance the Rapper">Chance the Rapper</a> and <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a>, were confirmed as judges for the <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Rhythm_%2B_Flow" title="Rhythm + Flow">Rhythm + Flow</a></i>, a ten-part hip-hop talent search that premiered on October 9, 2019, which she also <a href="/wiki/Executive_producer" title="Executive producer">executive produced</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hollywood_Reporter_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2019, Cardi B embarked on her first tour of Africa, performing in Nigeria and Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Her collaboration "<a href="/wiki/Clout_(Offset_song)" title="Clout (Offset song)">Clout</a>" was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Performance">Grammy Award for Best Rap Performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> She was the most streamed female rapper of 2019 in the US, according to Spotify.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Consequence_of_Sound" class="mw-redirect" title="Consequence of Sound">Consequence of Sound</a></i> deemed her "one of the most formidable hip-hop artists of the decade."<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In March 2020, Cardi B created a reaction video about the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">coronavirus pandemic</a>. DJ iMarkkeyz, a Brooklyn DJ known for turning memes and online moments into full-length songs, created a track, based on her reaction titled "Coronavirus", which became an <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">internet meme</a> and was released to music platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Netflix announced the return of <i>Rhythm + Flow</i> for 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B released the single "<a href="/wiki/WAP_(song)" title="WAP (song)">WAP</a>" featuring American rapper <a href="/wiki/Megan_Thee_Stallion" title="Megan Thee Stallion">Megan Thee Stallion</a> on August 7, 2020, as the lead single off her forthcoming second studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The song received critical acclaim and was praised for its <a href="/wiki/Sex-positive_movement" title="Sex-positive movement">sex positive</a> messages.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Colin_Tilley" title="Colin Tilley">Colin Tilley</a>-directed music video accompanied the song itself, and broke the record for the biggest 24-hour debut for an all-female collaboration on YouTube.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> She became the only female rap artist to top the Global Spotify chart multiple times.<sup id="cite_ref-streaming_wap_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-streaming_wap-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> "WAP" debuted at number-one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, garnering Cardi B her fourth chart-topper in the US, extending her record as the female rapper with the most number-one singles, and also making her the first female rapper to achieve Hot 100 number one singles in two different decades (2010s and 2020s).<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-streaming_wap_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-streaming_wap-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With 93&#160;million streaming units, it became the largest first-week streams for a song, breaking the all-time record held by <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/7_Rings" title="7 Rings">7 Rings</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> It has spent four weeks atop the Hot 100. The single has also spent multiple weeks at number one in seven other countries, including Australia and the United Kingdom. Neil Shah of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> deemed it "a big moment for female rappers" and "a historic sign that women artists are making their mark on hip-hop like never before".<sup id="cite_ref-wsj_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> "WAP" became the first number one single on the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Global_200" title="Billboard Global 200"><i>Billboard</i> Global 200</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It became critics' best song of the year according to a compilation of rankings made by the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> with publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> placing it at number one. Cardi B won the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award_for_Top_Rap_Female_Artist" title="Billboard Music Award for Top Rap Female Artist"><i>Billboard</i> Music Award for Top Rap Female Artist</a> for the third time at the <a href="/wiki/2020_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2020 Billboard Music Awards">2020 ceremony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In December 2020, Cardi B became the first female rapper to be named <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music#Woman_of_the_Year_Award" title="Billboard Women in Music">Woman of the Year</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music" title="Billboard Women in Music"><i>Billboard</i> Women in Music</a> Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> With her win for "WAP" at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, she became the first artist to win the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award_for_Favorite_Rap/Hip-Hop_Song" class="mw-redirect" title="American Music Award for Favorite Rap/Hip-Hop Song">American Music Award for Favorite Rap/Hip-Hop Song</a> multiple times, following her win for "Bodak Yellow" in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2021.E2.80.93present:_Upcoming_second_studio_album"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2021–present:_Upcoming_second_studio_album">2021–present: Upcoming second studio album</span></h3>
<p>On February 5, 2021, Cardi B released "<a href="/wiki/Up_(Cardi_B_song)" title="Up (Cardi B song)">Up</a>", the second single from her upcoming studio album. A music video for the single was released alongside it. The song was praised by <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> magazine for its lyricism and fresh approach as a successor to "WAP".<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> "Up" debuted at number two on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, marking the highest debut for a solo female rap song since <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Doo_Wop_(That_Thing)" title="Doo Wop (That Thing)">Doo Wop (That Thing)</a>" in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The song debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_charts" title="Rolling Stone charts"><i>Rolling Stone</i> Top 100</a>, becoming both Cardi B's second number-one single and second number-one debut, as well as the first time a female rapper debuts atop the chart with a solo song.<sup id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Cardidi B became the first female artist and first lead artist with consecutive number-one debuts on the US <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart, and second overall performer following <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> "Up" reached number one on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 after her <a href="/wiki/63rd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="63rd Annual Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> performance, making Cher he only female rapper to reach number one multiple times with solo songs, following "<a href="/wiki/Bodak_Yellow" title="Bodak Yellow">Bodak Yellow</a>", and extended her record as the female rapper with the most number-one songs on the Hot 100 as her fifth chart-topper.<sup id="cite_ref-up_number_one_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-up_number_one-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B received a second nomination for the <a href="/wiki/Brit_Award_for_International_Female_Solo_Artist" title="Brit Award for International Female Solo Artist">Brit Award for International Female Solo Artist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B made a last-minute appearance in "Big Paper", from DJ Khaled's album <i><a href="/wiki/Khaled_Khaled" title="Khaled Khaled">Khaled Khaled</a></i> released on April 30, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Cardi received two nominations for the <a href="/wiki/BET_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year" title="BET Award for Video of the Year">BET Award for Video of the Year</a>, for the videos "Up" and "WAP", winning for the latter and becoming the first female rapper to win Video of the Year as a lead artist. This became the 10th time that an artist has had two nominated videos in this category as a lead artist, and the second time for her, following her nominations for "Money" and "Please Me" in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She announced her second pregnancy during the performance of her Migos collaboration "Type Shit" at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_2021" title="BET Awards 2021">2021 ceremony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> She also appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/F9_(film)" title="F9 (film)">F9</a></i>, which was released on June 25, 2021, by <a href="/wiki/Universal_Pictures" title="Universal Pictures">Universal Pictures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> On July 16, 2021, Cardi B was featured on the <a href="/wiki/Normani" title="Normani">Normani</a> single "<a href="/wiki/Wild_Side_(Normani_song)" title="Wild Side (Normani song)">Wild Side</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Cardi collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Lizzo" title="Lizzo">Lizzo</a> on "<a href="/wiki/Rumors_(Lizzo_song)" title="Rumors (Lizzo song)">Rumors</a>", which debuted at number four on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, becoming Cardi B's tenth top 10 single on the chart, and her seventh number-one on the Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs chart.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B received six nominations at the <a href="/wiki/2021_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2021 MTV Video Music Awards">2021 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, including her second nomination for Video of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> She also led the nominations for the <a href="/wiki/2021_BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="2021 BET Hip Hop Awards">2021 BET Hip Hop Awards</a> along with Megan Thee Stallion, with nine each;<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> both rappers won the most awards during the ceremony with three for "WAP", with Cardi becoming the first female artist to win Best Hip Hop Video twice (2019 and 2021).<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 28, 2021, Cardi B previewed her second album to Atlantic Records via her Instagram Story. She captioned "The money people liking the album sounds".<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> On November 2, Cardi B was announced as the host of the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2021" title="American Music Awards of 2021">2021 American Music Awards</a> (AMAs). The award show was held at the Microsoft Theater in Los Angeles on November 21,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and marked the most social telecast of the year per interactions across social media.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> During the ceremony, "Up" won the award for <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award_for_Favorite_Rap/Hip_Hop_Song" title="American Music Award for Favorite Rap/Hip Hop Song">Favorite Hip Hop Song</a>, making Cardi B the first artist to win the category three times.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B featured on <a href="/wiki/Summer_Walker" title="Summer Walker">Summer Walker</a>'s 2021 album <i><a href="/wiki/Still_Over_It" title="Still Over It">Still Over It</a></i> on the opening track "Bitter".<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Warner Records released the soundtrack for <a href="/wiki/Halle_Berry" title="Halle Berry">Halle Berry</a>'s directorial debut film <i><a href="/wiki/Bruised_(film)" title="Bruised (film)">Bruised</a></i> on November 19. Selected by executive producers Berry and Cardi B, the Netflix film's soundtrack features six original songs by female artists, including Cardi, <a href="/wiki/H.E.R." title="H.E.R.">H.E.R.</a>, City Girls, <a href="/wiki/Flo_Milli" title="Flo Milli">Flo Milli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saweetie" title="Saweetie">Saweetie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Latto" title="Latto">Latto</a>, and seven additional female rap songs inspired by the film.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2022, Cardi B appeared on the extended version of Summer Walker and <a href="/wiki/SZA" title="SZA">SZA</a>'s collaboration, "<a href="/wiki/No_Love_(Summer_Walker_and_SZA_song)" title="No Love (Summer Walker and SZA song)">No Love</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The following month, she featured on rapper Kay Flock's song, "<a href="/wiki/Shake_It_(Kay_Flock_song)" title="Shake It (Kay Flock song)">Shake It</a>"; it samples <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a>'s 2005 song "<a href="/wiki/Belly_Dancer_(Bananza)" title="Belly Dancer (Bananza)">Belly Dancer (Bananza)</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> On July 1, 2022, Cardi B released "<a href="/wiki/Hot_Shit_(song)" title="Hot Shit (song)">Hot Shit</a>", featuring rappers <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Durk" title="Lil Durk">Lil Durk</a>, as the third single from her upcoming second studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> On July 8 and 9, she headlined the 2022 <a href="/wiki/Wireless_Festival" title="Wireless Festival">Wireless Festival</a> in London and <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The song was first announced during a <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_2022" title="BET Awards 2022">BET Awards 2022</a> commercial break.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B worked with rapper <a href="/wiki/GloRilla" title="GloRilla">GloRilla</a> on the remix to her song "Tomorrow" titled "<a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_(GloRilla_song)#Tomorrow_2" title="Tomorrow (GloRilla song)">Tomorrow 2</a>", which was released in September 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The remix peaked at number 9 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, becoming Cardi's eleventh top-ten single on the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/HipHopDX" title="HipHopDX">HipHopDX</a></i> listed it as the Best Hip-Hop Collaboration of 2022 while it was also the highest-listed by a female rapper on <i>Billboard</i>'s 100 Best Songs of 2022 list.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> On October 1, Cardi B made a surprise appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">Inglewood</a> show of Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Bad_Bunny" title="Bad Bunny">Bad Bunny</a>'s concert tour, the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Hottest_Tour" title="World&#39;s Hottest Tour">World's Hottest Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> In November, she signed with entertainment executive <a href="/wiki/Irving_Azoff" title="Irving Azoff">Irving Azoff</a>'s Full Stop Management.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B confirmed that her second studio album would be released in 2023, revealing that she had "no choice". She stated that she felt indecisive as the record was "missing something".<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> On December 3, 2022, she gave a 35-minute private performance at the <a href="/wiki/Art_Basel#Miami_Beach,_Florida" title="Art Basel">Miami Art Basel</a> for which she was paid $1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Also in December, the rapper featured on the remix of Spanish artist <a href="/wiki/Rosal%C3%ADa" title="Rosalía">Rosalía</a>'s song, "<a href="/wiki/Despech%C3%A1" title="Despechá">Despechá</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B appeared as a surprise performer at the New York City shows of SZA and GloRilla's tours: the <a href="/wiki/SOS_Tour" title="SOS Tour">SOS Tour</a> and Anyways, Life's Great Tour, in early 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> In March 2023, it was announced that Cardi B, along with Offset and two of their children, joined the voice cast of the children's animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Baby_Shark%27s_Big_Show!#Film" title="Baby Shark&#39;s Big Show!">Baby Shark's Big Movie</a></i>, set to be released on <a href="/wiki/Paramount%2B" title="Paramount+">Paramount+</a> later this year.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> In April, she served as one of three headliners of the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Loud" title="Rolling Loud">Rolling Loud Thailand</a> festival in <a href="/wiki/Pattaya" title="Pattaya">Pattaya</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown" title="Chris Brown">Chris Brown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> In June, she featured on "Put It on da Floor Again", the remix to rapper Latto's "<a href="/wiki/Put_It_on_da_Floor" title="Put It on da Floor">Put It on da Floor</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> It peaked at number 13 on the Hot 100, becoming Cardi's 20th top-twenty single on the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> On June 4, Cardi B headlined the 2023 <a href="/wiki/Summer_Jam_(festival)" title="Summer Jam (festival)">Summer Jam</a> festival in <a href="/wiki/Elmont,_New_York" title="Elmont, New York">Elmont, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> ln July, she featured on "<a href="/wiki/Point_Me_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Point Me 2">Point Me 2</a>", the remix to drill rapper FendiDa Rappa's single "Point Me to the Slut's".<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Her next collaboration was "<a href="/wiki/Jealousy_(Offset_and_Cardi_B_song)" title="Jealousy (Offset and Cardi B song)">Jealousy</a>" with Offset, released later that month, which samples <a href="/wiki/Three_6_Mafia" title="Three 6 Mafia">Three 6 Mafia</a>'s "Jealous Ass Bitches".<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h3><p>
In <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s "You Should Know" series, Cardi B said the first albums she ever purchased were by American entertainers <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tweet_(singer)" title="Tweet (singer)">Tweet</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-five_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-five-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> She has credited Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Ivy_Queen" title="Ivy Queen">Ivy Queen</a><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> and Jamaican dancehall artist <a href="/wiki/Spice_(musician)" title="Spice (musician)">Spice</a><sup id="cite_ref-igspice_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-igspice-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> as influences, as well as <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim" title="Lil&#39; Kim">Lil' Kim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madonna" title="Madonna">Madonna</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Decker_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decker-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Selena" title="Selena">Selena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> She has mentioned <a href="/wiki/Drill_music" title="Drill music">Chicago drill music</a> as an important influence.<sup id="cite_ref-bbwoty_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbwoty-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> When asked about the initial direction for her music, Cardi B said in an interview, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"When I first started rapping [...] I liked certain songs from <a href="/wiki/Khia" title="Khia">Khia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trina" title="Trina">Trina</a>, and they [were] fighting songs. I haven't heard fighting songs for a very long time," crediting the two female rappers for her aggressive rap style.
