She continued, saying "a lot of girls they cannot afford <a href="/wiki/Christian_Louboutin" title="Christian Louboutin">red bottoms</a>, a lot of girls they cannot afford foreign cars [...] but I know that every girl has beef with a girl [...] I know that every bitch don't like some bitch, and it's like 'that's what I wanna rap about.'"<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p> She also credits growing up in the South Bronx and real life experiences as influences for her songwriting; "I wouldn't be able to rap about the things that I rap about now [if I hadn't grown up there]."<sup id="cite_ref-Decker_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decker-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span></h3>
<p>Her first studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Privacy_(album)" title="Invasion of Privacy (album)">Invasion of Privacy</a></i>, is primarily a <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> record, which comprises elements of <a href="/wiki/Trap_music_(hip_hop)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trap music (hip hop)">trap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_music" title="Latin music">Latin music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tnyt_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tnyt-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Consequence_of_Sound" class="mw-redirect" title="Consequence of Sound">Consequence of Sound</a></i> described her flow as "acrobatic and nimble."<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> editor David Jeffries called Cardi B "a raw and aggressive rapper".<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stereogum" title="Stereogum">Stereogum</a> called her voice "a full-bodied New Yawk nasal bleat, the sort of thing that you've heard if someone has ever told you that you stupid for taking too long at swiping your <a href="/wiki/MetroCard_(New_York_City)" class="mw-redirect" title="MetroCard (New York City)">MetroCard</a>." They continued to call her voice "an unabashedly loud and sexual fuck-you New York honk—that translates perfectly to rap."<sup id="cite_ref-Stereog_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stereog-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 2017 <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> article about her, the editor wrote "unapologetic does not begin to describe the totally unfiltered and sheer Cardi B-ness of Cardi B's personality. She's a hood chick who's not afraid to be hood no matter the setting. Cardi B is Cardi B <a href="/wiki/24/7_service" title="24/7 service">24/7, 365</a>, this is why she resonates with people, and that same energy comes out in her music."<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Her <a href="/wiki/Flow_(rapping)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flow (rapping)">flow</a> has been described as aggressive<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, <i>NME</i> described her lyrics as "sexually free" performed with "rapid" flow,<sup id="cite_ref-nme_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nme-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> and other publications have further described her lyrics as outspoken,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> while her punchlines have been praised, by such publications as <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)"><i>Pitchfork</i></a> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source" title="The Source">The Source</a></i>, as clever and quotable.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> She possesses a <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Americans#New_York_City" title="Dominican Americans">New York-Dominican</a> accent.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B has defended her musical content featuring sexually-charged lyrics—like most contemporary female rappers; she stated that the content "seems like that's what people want to hear", since she faced negative reactions after releasing her more emotional song, "<a href="/wiki/Be_Careful_(Cardi_B_song)" title="Be Careful (Cardi B song)">Be Careful</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> She has declared, "[Drill music] is the type of artist I always wanted to be: I like to rap about the streets, and I like to rap about my pussy. I don't give a fuck about it."<sup id="cite_ref-bbwoty_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbwoty-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> She has stated that writing and performing songs about her personal life and relationships initially caused her a "weird and uncomfortable" feeling and shyness.<sup id="cite_ref-bbwoty_217-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbwoty-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B employs different vocal styles in her music; in "WAP" her vocal performance has been described as "throaty"<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> and "staccato",<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> while in "Up" she raps with <a href="/wiki/Alliteration" title="Alliteration">alliteration</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tongue_twister" title="Tongue twister">tongue twister</a>-run, and "some classically comedic Cardi" <a href="/wiki/Punch_line" title="Punch line">punch lines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span></h2>
<p>In February 2017, she partnered with <a href="/wiki/MAC_Cosmetics" title="MAC Cosmetics">M.A.C</a> and Rio Uribe's Gypsy Sport for an event for <a href="/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week" title="New York Fashion Week">New York Fashion Week</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYFW_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYFW-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Her April appearance in <i><a href="/wiki/I-D" title="I-D">i-D</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s "A-Z of Music" video was sponsored by designer <a href="/wiki/Marc_Jacobs" title="Marc Jacobs">Marc Jacobs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and she made the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fader" title="The Fader">The Fader</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s July/August 2017 Summer Music issue.<sup id="cite_ref-ww_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Ford" title="Tom Ford">Tom Ford</a>'s Cardi B-inspired lipstick, and named after her, was released in September 2018. It sold out within 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> In November, she released a clothing line collection with <a href="/wiki/Fashion_Nova" title="Fashion Nova">Fashion Nova</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> The same month she partnered with <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a>, promoting the brand's Aztrek sneaker.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> In partnership with Reebok, she released a footwear and apparel collection in 2020, inspired by her personal style and paying homage to "classic 80s styling" and motifs.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> She released her second collection with Reebok in 2021, including sneakers, tracksuits and corsets, inspired by everyday life in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> The fourth collection with the brand was released in September 2022, titled "Let Me Be...Next Level Energy". Inspired by Cardi B's "unmatched energy", the collection includes crop tops, sneakers, bodysuits, leggings, and woven jackets; its color palette is based on <a href="/wiki/Crystal" title="Crystal">crystals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Her fifth and final collection with Reebok, a second edition of "Next Level Energy", was released in December 2022, bringing an end to her four-year partnership with the brand.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> for three television commercials, which aired during the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LIII" title="Super Bowl LIII">Super Bowl LIII</a>, the <a href="/wiki/61st_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="61st Annual Grammy Awards">61st Annual Grammy Awards</a>, and Christmas.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> In early 2019, Cardi also joined other hip hop artists (including her husband <a href="/wiki/Offset_(rapper)" title="Offset (rapper)">Offset</a>, as part of <a href="/wiki/Migos" title="Migos">Migos</a>) in releasing her flavors of snack food Rap Snacks: two flavors of chips, and two of popcorn. The bags' artwork were designed by Jai Manselle and inspired by the cover of <i>Invasion of Privacy</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She premiered the series <i>Cardi Tries</i> via <a href="/wiki/Facebook_Messenger" class="mw-redirect" title="Facebook Messenger">Facebook Messenger</a> in December 2020, with herself as one of the executive producers.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> The web series ran for three seasons until 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2021, Cardi B partnered with <a href="/wiki/Playboy_Enterprises" class="mw-redirect" title="Playboy Enterprises">PLBY Group Inc.</a> as <a href="/wiki/Creative_director" title="Creative director">creative director</a> in residence for <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i> and founding member of Centerfold, a creator-driven website in the works. The partnership also includes fashion and sexual-wellness products.<sup id="cite_ref-playboy_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-playboy-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> In collaboration with Starco Brands, she launched a <a href="/wiki/Vodka" title="Vodka">vodka</a>-infused, <a href="/wiki/Vegan" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegan">vegan</a> whipped cream "Whipshots" the same month.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> It has sold over two million cans as of March 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2023, Cardi B and Offset partnered with <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a> to create the Cardi B and Offset meal which was launched on <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine&#39;s Day">Valentine's Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> The meal was first announced in the 2023 McDonald's <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_commercials" title="Super Bowl commercials">Super Bowl commercial</a> which the couple appeared in.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h3>
<p>In 2022, Cardi B donated $100,000 to the elementary school she attended, I.S. 232 in the Bronx.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_statements">Political statements</span></h3>
<p>Cardi B identifies as a <a href="/wiki/Feminist" class="mw-redirect" title="Feminist">feminist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> The rapper has been called "unabashedly, directly political"<sup id="cite_ref-:2_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and often uses social media to advocate for causes she believes in, such as <a href="/wiki/Gun_control" title="Gun control">gun control</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 presidential primaries</a>, she warned her fans of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">President Trump</a>'s immigration policies and encouraged them to vote for Senator <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders" title="Bernie Sanders">Bernie Sanders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/60th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="60th Annual Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> in 2018, she appeared in a video along with <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> to narrate a portion of <i><a href="/wiki/Fire_and_Fury" title="Fire and Fury">Fire and Fury</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wolff_(journalist)" title="Michael Wolff (journalist)">Michael Wolff</a>'s insider's account of Trump's administration, and stated "Why am I even reading this shit? I can't believe this. I can't believe—this is how he really lives his life?"<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Early in 2018 she used her social media to demand transparency on <a href="/wiki/Tax_policy" title="Tax policy">tax policy</a>, asking for detailed information on how her taxpayer dollars are being spent in New York state and criticizing the maintenance of its streets, prisons, and <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Transportation_Authority" title="Metropolitan Transportation Authority">public transportation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B endorsed Sanders once again in his <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders_2020_presidential_campaign" title="Bernie Sanders 2020 presidential campaign">second bid</a> for the presidency in the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election" title="2020 United States presidential election">2020 United States presidential election</a>, while praising U.S. Representative <a href="/wiki/Tim_Ryan_(Ohio_politician)" title="Tim Ryan (Ohio politician)">Tim Ryan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> She stated that one of the reasons for her endorsement is Sanders' long-time involvement in supporting underprivileged minorities and "people getting <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(United_States)" title="Medicare (United States)">Medicare</a> because he knows they can't afford it,"<sup id="cite_ref-vogue_cover_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue_cover-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Politico" title="Politico">Politico</a> argued that she "might be one of Bernie's most powerful 2020 allies."<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She has used her social pages to raise awareness for victims of <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality" title="Police brutality">police brutality</a>, and has encouraged people to vote for mayors, judges and <a href="/wiki/District_attorney" title="District attorney">district attorneys</a> in local elections.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> In a conversation with Democratic candidate <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Elle_(magazine)" title="Elle (magazine)">Elle</a></i>, they discussed Medicare, <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free college tuition</a>, and racial equality.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> According to a study published by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i>, Cardi B ranked as the fifth most influential celebrity, and fourth among <a href="/wiki/Generation_Z" title="Generation Z">Generation Z</a>, for the 2020 presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She has praised President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> for advocating for the <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a> program and the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> She said of President Roosevelt, "he helped us get over the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Depression</a>, all while he was in a wheelchair. Like, this man was suffering from <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a> at the time of his presidency, and yet all he was worried about was trying to make America great—make America great again for real. He's the real 'Make America Great Again,' because if it wasn't for him, old people wouldn't even get Social Security."<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Sanders has praised her for her "leading role" in calling attention to Social Security.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardi_B_at_Vogue_Taiwan_(2).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Cardi_B_at_Vogue_Taiwan_%282%29.jpg/220px-Cardi_B_at_Vogue_Taiwan_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Cardi_B_at_Vogue_Taiwan_%282%29.jpg/330px-Cardi_B_at_Vogue_Taiwan_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Cardi_B_at_Vogue_Taiwan_%282%29.jpg/440px-Cardi_B_at_Vogue_Taiwan_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1070" data-file-height="720" /></a><figcaption>Cardi B doing <a href="/wiki/ASMR" title="ASMR">ASMR</a> during an interview with <i>Vogue</i></figcaption></figure>
<p>Cardi has a noted affinity for <a href="/wiki/Christian_Louboutin" title="Christian Louboutin">Christian Louboutin</a> heels, a running theme in her song "Bodak Yellow".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> She has also mentioned her affinity for cheap, <a href="/wiki/Fast_fashion" title="Fast fashion">fast fashion</a> brands stating "I don't care if it cost $20 or $15. If it looks good on me, it looks good on me".<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> During an interview in early 2017, Cardi B spoke on being rejected by some fashion designers.<sup id="cite_ref-bb_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bb-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> Cardi wore vintage <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Mugler" title="Thierry Mugler">Thierry Mugler</a> to the <a href="/wiki/2019_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 Grammy Awards">2019 Grammy Awards</a>, with an <i><a href="/wiki/I-D" title="I-D">i-D</a></i> article stating that the fashion house's "resurgence onto the fashion scene can almost single-handedly be attributed" to the <a href="/wiki/Swarovski_crystal" class="mw-redirect" title="Swarovski crystal">Swarovski crystal</a>-embroidered crinoline sheath gown she wore at the ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-i-d.vice.com_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-d.vice.com-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mugler's collaboration with Cardi B marked the second time in 25 years that the Paris house opened its archives to dress a celebrity, the first being <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> for her 2009 concert tour.<sup id="cite_ref-i-d.vice.com_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-d.vice.com-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/W_(magazine)" title="W (magazine)"><i>W</i></a> magazine credited the "WAP" music video for popularizing the Mugler bodysuit in the mainstream.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Cardi has acknowledged Mugler as one of the first designers to "take a major chance on [her]" for their fashion collaborations.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(magazine)" title="Vogue (magazine)">Vogue</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> have referred to her as a <a href="/wiki/Fashion_icon" title="Fashion icon">fashion icon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> An article from <i>Vogue</i> noted she "is famous for her statement getups—whether she's rocking archival Mugler on the red carpet, or dripping in Chanel while sitting courtside at a basketball game."<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> Her over-the-top manicures, designed by <a href="/wiki/Nail_artist" class="mw-redirect" title="Nail artist">nail artist</a> <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Bui" title="Jenny Bui">Jenny Bui</a> and studded with <a href="/wiki/Swarovski_crystals" class="mw-redirect" title="Swarovski crystals">Swarovski crystals</a>, has become a part of her signature look.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> Editor Christian Allaire from the magazine in 2021 commented that her signature "bold" ensembles "create a spectacle" during <a href="/wiki/Fashion_week" title="Fashion week">fashion weeks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, she became the first female rapper in the US to appear on the cover of <i>Vogue</i> magazine. Photographed by <a href="/wiki/Annie_Leibovitz" title="Annie Leibovitz">Annie Leibovitz</a>, the cover, one of four for the January 2019 issue that included <a href="/wiki/Stella_McCartney" title="Stella McCartney">Stella McCartney</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> features her in a red and white <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kors" title="Michael Kors">Michael Kors</a> dress and matching red <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Choo" title="Jimmy Choo">Jimmy Choo</a> shoes, while holding her daughter, Kulture.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Fashion_Designers_of_America" title="Council of Fashion Designers of America">Council of Fashion Designers of America</a> included her on their list of "28 Black Fashion Forces".<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> <i>Vogue</i> editor-in-chief <a href="/wiki/Anna_Wintour" title="Anna Wintour">Anna Wintour</a> commended her fashion sense, declaring that she "completely rethought [her] opinion of Cardi B's style" after the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Met_Gala" title="Met Gala">Met Gala</a>, where the rapper wore a <a href="/wiki/Thom_Browne" title="Thom Browne">Thom Browne</a>-designed burgundy gown that extends outward in concentric circles for about ten feet and was inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Female_body_shape" title="Female body shape">female form</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B became the face of <a href="/wiki/Balenciaga" title="Balenciaga">Balenciaga</a>'s ad campaign for the winter 2020 season. The campaign includes billboards in several international locations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Louvre" title="Louvre">Louvre</a> museum. <i>Vogue</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Brooke Bobb commented, "This is Cardi's first campaign for a luxury fashion house, though she's definitely no stranger to the Parisian style scene", citing her floral printed <a href="/wiki/Richard_Quinn_(designer)" title="Richard Quinn (designer)">Richard Quinn</a> ensemble "that literally covered her from head to toe" and her being "a front row fixture" at <a href="/wiki/High_fashion" class="mw-redirect" title="High fashion">high fashion</a> shows, adding, "She and her stylist Kollin Carter have been wildly successful in carving out a much-needed space for Cardi within the fashion industry, and they've cultivated a personal style that is all her own while being inspiring to all".<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, Cardi B became the first female rapper to be awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Footwear_News" title="Footwear News">FN Achievement Awards</a> when she won the Style Influencer of the Year award, which was presented to her by <a href="/wiki/Christian_Louboutin" title="Christian Louboutin">Christian Louboutin</a>. In a press release for the awards show, she was called an "influence just about everything in pop culture—from music, fashion and style to social media, politics and even public service".<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> In 2022, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked her as the second most-stylish woman in music, behind <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> considered her "one of fashion's preeminent risk-takers."<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span></h2>
<p>Cardi B has been referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Reigning Queen of Hip Hop</a>" by multiple publications, including <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Omaha_World-Herald" title="Omaha World-Herald">Omaha World-Herald</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Enterprise" title="Black Enterprise">Black Enterprise</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hollywood_Reporter_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> and as the "Queen of Rap" by <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Essence_(magazine)" title="Essence (magazine)">Essence</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Bazaar" title="Harper&#39;s Bazaar">Harper's Bazaar Malaysia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jakarta_Post" title="The Jakarta Post">The Jakarta Post</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Uproxx" title="Uproxx">Uproxx</a>, <a href="/wiki/IHeartRadio" title="IHeartRadio">iHeartRadio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geo_TV" title="Geo TV">Geo TV</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Joe_(website)" title="Joe (website)">Joe</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_Herald" title="Boston Herald">Boston Herald</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Refinery_29" class="mw-redirect" title="Refinery 29">Refinery 29</a>, <a href="/wiki/France_24" title="France 24">France 24</a>, and Nigerian media <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_(Nigeria)" title="The Guardian (Nigeria)">The Guardian</a></i>,  <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Media_Trust" title="Media Trust">Daily Trust</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nme_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nme-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> staff credited her for opening "the table to a new generation of pop artists remaking American music in their own image and accents," as Cardi B "recognized that <a href="/wiki/Person_of_color" title="Person of color">POC</a> artists no longer need to pander or soften themselves in order to become household names."<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> editors stated that with "Bodak Yellow"'s commercial success, "she left an indelible mark on the summer of 2017, not only because she rewrote history, but she gave hope to the have nots...".<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> Several publications have credited "I Like It", the first <a href="/wiki/Latin_trap" title="Latin trap">Latin trap</a> song to reach number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a>, for introducing the "musical movement" to a mainstream, massive audience.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Carl Lamarre considered "WAP"'s achievements "a clever Trojan horse for the myriad ways Cardi influences the culture with every move she makes."<sup id="cite_ref-bbwoty_217-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbwoty-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Neil Shah stated in 2020 that her breakthrough and success influenced "today's female-rap renaissance," while <a href="/wiki/Genius_(website)" class="mw-redirect" title="Genius (website)">Genius</a> staff credited her for "helping jumpstart a new wave of female hip-hop signings and promotion at labels,"<sup id="cite_ref-wsj_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/NPR_Music" title="NPR Music">NPR Music</a> commented that the "renaissance" of the dynamism of women in rap grew "in enthusiasm and breadth" since Cardi's "first historic run" in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Clover_Hope" title="Clover Hope">Clover Hope</a>'s book <i>The Motherlode</i> (2021) stated that <i>Invasion of Privacy</i> "jump-started a new era for women rappers in which success felt much more tangible" as Cardi B "multiplied the wealth of talent and resurrected the idea that numerous women who controlled their own stories could dominate rap at once."<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> has credited her for "changing a genre that has rarely allowed for more than one female superstar at a time."<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Uproxx" title="Uproxx">Uproxx</a></i> noted Cardi B for promoting up-and-coming female rappers; "[she is] choosing to use her position at the height of stardom to open doors for other women to flourish in hip-hop at a greater level than any since the <a href="/wiki/Golden_age_hip_hop" title="Golden age hip hop">Golden Era</a> and '<a href="/wiki/All_Hail_the_Queen" title="All Hail the Queen">Ladies First</a>'," considering it "something of a departure from tradition; for the decade previous to Cardi's precipitous come-up, it seemed hip-hop had an unspoken, <a href="/wiki/Highlander_(franchise)" title="Highlander (franchise)">Highlander</a>-esque rule in place regarding women."<sup id="cite_ref-cosign_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cosign-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> deemed her a "hip-hop icon",<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> called her "the people's pop culture icon", writing that she "has become one of the most recognisable cultural figures of the past 10 years".<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a> defined "Cardi B effect" as "a <a href="/wiki/Personal_branding" title="Personal branding">branding power</a> rooted in specific authenticity, created and permeated by rapper Cardi B" and noticed that with her breakthrough, "brands finally started to become hip to [her] effect, noticing the cultural markers outside of the rap world that were proving it wasn't limited to clubs, concerts and radio."<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> Business magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Inc._(magazine)" title="Inc. (magazine)">Inc.</a></i> stated that her success "shows how social media changed everything we knew about <a href="/wiki/Promotional_mix" title="Promotional mix">traditional marketing</a> and media", which no longer relies on a "well-thought marketing scheme or millions of dollars in advertising."<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, a life-sized sculpture of her was on display at the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a>, as part of <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a>'s RapCaviar "Pantheon".<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_News" title="Bloomberg News">Bloomberg</a> reported that her data bill helped to boost Ghana's GDP growth in 2019, after it was part of a concert tour.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> She inspired the creation of the sitcom <i>Partners in Rhyme</i>, executively produced by <a href="/wiki/MC_Lyte" title="MC Lyte">MC Lyte</a> about a young woman in high school who "aspires to be the next Cardi B."<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/P-Valley" title="P-Valley">P-Valley</a></i> creator and executive producer <a href="/wiki/Katori_Hall" title="Katori Hall">Katori Hall</a> cited her an inspiration for the TV series, and credited her for "helping prepare the public" for its storyline.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several artists have cited Cardi B's work as an inspiration, including <a href="/wiki/Rosal%C3%ADa_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosalía (singer)">Rosalía</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Rodrigo" title="Olivia Rodrigo">Olivia Rodrigo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jazmine_Sullivan" title="Jazmine Sullivan">Jazmine Sullivan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Blackpink" title="Blackpink">Blackpink</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Spice_(musician)" title="Spice (musician)">Spice</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-igspice_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-igspice-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greta_Gerwig" title="Greta Gerwig">Greta Gerwig</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nathy_Peluso" title="Nathy Peluso">Nathy Peluso</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rubi_Rose" title="Rubi Rose">Rubi Rose</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Becerra" title="María Becerra">María Becerra</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Abigail_Asante" title="Abigail Asante">Abigail Asante</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B has been credited for supporting and uniting female rappers in the industry,<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> with a writer from <i>Uproxx</i> considering her co-sign "the new <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a> effect" for women in hip hop.<sup id="cite_ref-cosign_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cosign-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Cardi_B" title="List of awards and nominations received by Cardi B">List of awards and nominations received by Cardi B</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardi_B_VMA_2018_(cropped).png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Cardi_B_VMA_2018_%28cropped%29.png/220px-Cardi_B_VMA_2018_%28cropped%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="211" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Cardi_B_VMA_2018_%28cropped%29.png/330px-Cardi_B_VMA_2018_%28cropped%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Cardi_B_VMA_2018_%28cropped%29.png/440px-Cardi_B_VMA_2018_%28cropped%29.png 2x" data-file-width="586" data-file-height="561" /></a><figcaption>Cardi B at the <a href="/wiki/2018_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2018 MTV Video Music Awards">2018 MTV Video Music Awards</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Cardi B is the recipient of numerous accolades, including a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>, eight <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" title="Billboard Music Awards"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a> (including three consecutive <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award_for_Top_Rap_Female_Artist" title="Billboard Music Award for Top Rap Female Artist">Top Rap Female Artist</a> wins), six <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> six <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, four <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, six <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a> (including <a href="/wiki/BET_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="BET Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>), and fourteen <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>. <i>Invasion of Privacy</i>—which made her the first female rapper to win the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Grammy Award for Best Rap Album</a> as a solo artist—became the first female rap album <a href="/wiki/Under_Construction_(Missy_Elliott_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Under Construction (Missy Elliott album)">in fifteen years</a> to be nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Grammy Award for Album of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iop_aoty_nom_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iop_aoty_nom-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> included her on their <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">annual list</a> of the 100 most influential people in the world in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-time_100_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time_100-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> She received the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">ASCAP</a> award for <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers#Awards" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">Songwriter of the Year</a> in 2019, becoming the first female rapper to win the award.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> She received the honor for the second time in 2020, making her the first female songwriter to win the award twice.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, Cardi B became the first female rapper to be named <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music#Woman_of_the_Year_Award" title="Billboard Women in Music">Woman of the Year</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music" title="Billboard Women in Music"><i>Billboard</i> Women in Music</a> Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B is the female rapper with the most <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> number one singles (5)<sup id="cite_ref-up_number_one_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-up_number_one-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> and the one with the most total weeks on the top position (16).<sup id="cite_ref-hot_100_11_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hot_100_11-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-up_number_one_169-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-up_number_one-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> "I Like It" became the first song led by a female rapper to surpass <a href="/wiki/List_of_most-streamed_songs_on_Spotify" class="mw-redirect" title="List of most-streamed songs on Spotify">a billion streams</a> on <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a>, making her the first woman in hip hop with multiple billion-streamers on the service, with a total of three so far.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> With the singles "Taki Taki" and "WAP" she became the only female rapper to top the global Spotify chart multiple times.<sup id="cite_ref-streaming_wap_154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-streaming_wap-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Since August 2020, "WAP" holds the record of the biggest first-week streams for a song in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-streaming_wap_154-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-streaming_wap-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> <i>Invasion of Privacy</i> was the top female rap album of the 2010s, according to the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> decade-end chart.<sup id="cite_ref-iop_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iop-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> It became the longest-charting album by a female rapper on the <i>Billboard</i> 200,<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> and the most-streamed female rap album on Spotify.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi is the female rapper with the most <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification#RIAA_Diamond_certifications" title="RIAA certification">Diamond-certified</a> songs by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) (3): "Bodak Yellow", which made her the first female rapper to have a song certified Diamond; "<a href="/wiki/Girls_Like_You" title="Girls Like You">Girls Like You</a>", which made her the only female rapper to achieve multiple Diamond-certified songs; and "I Like It", a tie for the most among women artists.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-riaa_list_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa_list-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B has topped twice <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)#Pitchfork_awards" title="Pitchfork (website)">annual list of best songs of the year</a> (2017 and 2020).<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> staff and <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked her debut album number 13 and 34 on their critics' lists of the best albums of the 2010s respectively, both the highest rank for a female rapper for the decade.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B has become the highest-certified female rapper of all time on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-certified_music_artists_in_the_United_States" title="List of highest-certified music artists in the United States">RIAA's Top Artists (Digital Singles)</a> ranking, with 54 million certified units, also being among the highest-certified female artists overall.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa_list_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa_list-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In October, 2022, five years after her major-label debut, she reached 100 million units sold in RIAA certifications, across her album, singles and guest appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the US, Cardi has achieved three times the best-performing song of the year by a female artist—the first act to do so this century—in 2017, 2018, and 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> As of 2021, "I Like It" is the most-streamed song by a female rapper in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> In August 2021, "Bodak Yellow" made Cardi B the only female rapper to have two videos on her <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel with more than 1 billion views, joining "I Like It", and became the fastest solo female rap song to reach that mark on the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-allhiphop_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allhiphop-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vibe_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> Cardi is the only female rapper ranked on <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Greatest Hot 100 Hits of All Time, with "Girls Like You" at number 30.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Cardi B defined herself as a practicing <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup> In 2016 Cardi B said that, while working as a stripper during her younger years, she used to drug and rob men to get money.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc_explains_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_explains-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup> Following controversies on the matter, sparked in 2019, she defended herself by saying that she took money from them because they "wasted her time by falling asleep", and then "kept coming back."<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>She identifies as <a href="/wiki/Bisexuality" title="Bisexuality">bisexual</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> In connection with the <a href="/wiki/Me_Too_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Me Too movement">Me Too movement</a>, she has discussed being sexually assaulted in the past while working as a stripper.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
In a 2018 interview, Cardi B talked about being <a href="/wiki/Afro-Latin_Americans" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Latin Americans">Afro-Latina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Caribbean">Afro-Caribbean</a>:<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We are Caribbean people. [...] Some people want to decide if you're black or not, depending on your skin complexion, because they don't understand Caribbean people or our culture. [...] I don't got to tell you that I'm black. I expect you to know about it. When my father taught me about Caribbean countries, he told me that Europeans took over our lands. That's why we all speak different languages. [...] Just like everybody else, we came over here the same way. I hate when people try to take my roots from me. Because we know that there's African roots inside of us.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships">Relationships</span></h3>
<p>As of early 2017, Cardi B began dating fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Offset_(rapper)" title="Offset (rapper)">Offset</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_67-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fader1_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fader1-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> They became engaged on October 27, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> On April 7, 2018, during her second performance on <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, Cardi B revealed her pregnancy; she was about six months (24 weeks) pregnant at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> On June 25, 2018, <a href="/wiki/TMZ" title="TMZ">TMZ</a> found a marriage license revealing Cardi B and Offset had actually secretly married in September 2017, one month before the public proposal. She later confirmed this in a social media post.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardi B gave birth to her daughter on July 10, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> In December 2018, she announced on <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> that she and Offset had separated, though the pair later reunited.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup> In February 2019, the couple made a public appearance for the Grammys.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> He accompanied her onstage during her acceptance speech for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2020, it was reported that Cardi B had filed for divorce from Offset,<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> but the following month it was revealed they were back together.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> In June 2021, Cardi B revealed she was pregnant with her second child, a boy.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> She gave birth to her son on September 4, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup> On the fifth anniversary of her marriage, Cardi B announced she is planning her official wedding.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span></h3>
<p>On October 1, 2018, Cardi B was accused of an alleged assault of two female bartenders.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> The victims claimed that Cardi B and her entourage "threw bottles and alcohol at them."<sup id="cite_ref-:4_380-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-380">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup> She denied involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup> She was charged with two <a href="/wiki/Misdemeanor" title="Misdemeanor">misdemeanors</a>: assault and reckless endangerment.<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B appeared in court for her arraignment on December 7, 2018, after she did not show up for the originally scheduled date due to a scheduling conflict, according to her attorney.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup> On June 21, 2019, a jury indicted Cardi B on 14 charges, including two counts of felony assault with intent to cause serious physical injury, stemming from the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-nbcncharge_385-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbcncharge-385">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup> She was arraigned on June 25, 2019, and pleaded not guilty on all charges.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup> On September 15, 2022, she pleaded guilty to third-degree assault and second-degree reckless endangerment, resulting in a sentence of 15&#160;days of community service.<sup id="cite_ref-assault_388-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-assault-388">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 24, 2022,  Cardi won a million-dollar defamation verdict against YouTuber Latasha Kebe (Tasha K) for waging a "malicious campaign" to hurt her reputation by posting false rumors. She stated that the lies had led her to contemplate suicide in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup> The jury issued a verdict that Cardi B had been defamed and awarded $1.25 million in damages.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup> Further proceedings brought the total fine against Kebe to $3.82 million.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 25, 2022, Cardi, her sister Hennessy, and Hennessy's girlfriend won a defamation lawsuit filed against them by three men over an incident at a Suffolk County beach.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span></h3>
<p>Cardi B sparked controversy after throwing one of her high heel shoes at and attempting to physically attack fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> at a <a href="/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week" title="New York Fashion Week">New York Fashion Week</a> after-party in September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup> Following the altercation, she alleged that Minaj had previously "<a href="/wiki/Like_button" title="Like button">liked</a>" social media comments that spoke negatively of Cardi B's ability to take care of her newborn daughter.<sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup> Minaj denied the allegations, and accused Cardi B of <a href="/wiki/Cyberbullying" title="Cyberbullying">cyberbullying</a> in a heated Instagram exchange from 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> Cardi B was on the cover of the 2019 spring fashion issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Bazaar" title="Harper&#39;s Bazaar">Harper's Bazaar</a></i>, which featured her in a <a href="/wiki/Cinderella" title="Cinderella">Cinderella</a>-themed photo shoot wearing a red gown and leaving a shoe behind. Some interpreted this as a reference to the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the release of "<a href="/wiki/Girls_(Rita_Ora_song)" title="Girls (Rita Ora song)">Girls</a>" in May 2018, a collaboration where she had a featured verse, Cardi B responded to accusations of the song trivializing and sexualizing <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> relationships; she tweeted, "We never try to cause harm or had bad intentions with the song." She went on to add, "I personally myself had experiences with other women."<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, a video where Cardi B stopped her performance to aggressively throw a microphone towards a fan who threw a drink at her, surfaced on the internet, leading to controversies.<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">&#91;404&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
